## VII. Kree Political Entanglements and the Supreme Intelligence (CM #41–46, sundry crossovers)

The middle period also contains the slow, ambivalent reconciliation with the Kree state. The Supreme Intelligence — the same entity that sentenced him to death and engineered the Rick-fusion — repeatedly re-enters the file as both adversary and employer of last resort. The subject's behavior with the Supreme Intelligence is one of the most analytically interesting patterns in the entire dossier.

He neither forgives nor refuses contact. He answers when called. He executes missions that align with his ethical commitments and declines those that do not, and he does this *without performance*. He does not lecture the Intelligence. He does not theatrically refuse. He simply does or does not. The Intelligence, for its part, learns to read him and to ask only what he will give. This is, in effect, the first sustained adult-to-adult relationship between a Kree subject and the Supreme Intelligence the file knows of, and it is structured by the *subject's* refusal to either capitulate or revolt.

The political read: the subject becomes, across the middle period, a *back-channel* between the Kree Empire and the cosmic-tier powers (Titan, the Skrull moderates, the Watcher class) that the Empire cannot openly engage. He is asked to do this work because no one else can. He does it because it reduces the casualty toll among populations he has elected to protect. He does not list it on any résumé because he has no résumé.

---

## VIII. The Drax Arc and the Cosmic-Tier Norm (CM, late Englehart and Wein issues)

Recurring engagements with Drax the Destroyer — a being literally manufactured to kill Thanos and incapable of the broader negotiation the subject specializes in — produce a contrast that the file marks as instructive. Drax cannot be reasoned with about his prey; the subject can be reasoned with about anything. The two cooperate operationally; they do not become close. Drax is, in effect, the man the subject might have become if Eon had not awakened him — a weaponized purpose without a wider ethical frame. The subject treats Drax with patience, never with condescension, and tries — across several encounters — to *expand Drax's frame*. He does not succeed. The file marks this as the first documented instance of the subject *failing as a mentor* and the response is characteristic: no self-recrimination, no abandonment of Drax, no reduction in willingness to cooperate. He simply notes the limit and works within it.

This is the operational stance he will hold toward Thanos himself in the final encounters: *expand the frame if possible; if not, work within the limit*. He is one of very few beings in the cosmic register who treats Thanos as a person with whom intellectual engagement is possible. This stance is forged across the middle period, in repeated lower-stakes encounters with beings — Drax, the various Kree loyalists, even Yon-Rogg's surviving partisans — whom others would simply destroy.

---

## IX. The Late Middle: Moench, Broderick, and the Quiet Years (CM #47–62)

The terminal stretch of the middle period is, in publication terms, the long fade — the book's sales declining, the writers cycling, the cosmic-tier crises somewhat less apocalyptic. From a behavioral-record standpoint, however, this is when the subject's pattern *settles into its final form* and becomes legible as a coherent life-shape rather than a sequence of crises.

What stabilizes in these issues:
- **Mission selection becomes principled rather than reactive.** The early middle was largely reactive — he responded to what arrived. The late middle shows him *electing* engagements: he picks up cases the Cosmic Awareness flags as undervalued by other powers, often involving small populations, lone individuals, off-axis injustices. Protector of the Universe, operationalized, turns out to mean *attending to what others overlook*. A surveillance file would log a marked shift in the geographic and demographic distribution of his engagements: less Manhattan, more Centauri-margin colonies, fringe Skrull settlements, isolated Kree outposts on disputed worlds.
- **Increasing solitude inside increasing competence.** Powers and judgment are at their peak; companionship is at its minimum. He spends entire arcs without sustained dialogue with anyone but Rick at swap-points. The Zone-time grows. The Earth-time shrinks. He is *condensing*.
- **The asceticism deepens.** He has, by the late middle, *eliminated almost every appetite that is not mission-relevant*. No documented romantic involvement after Una. No documented friendships of leisure. No collected objects. No place he calls home other than the implicit station in the Zone. The file does not read this as depression — affect remains modulated and warm where warmth is invited. It reads it as a *life pruned to its essential function*.
- **The mentorship pattern generalizes.** No longer focused on Carol or Rick alone, his late-middle engagements increasingly involve brief, intense instruction of beings he meets in the field: a young Kree dissident here, a Rigellian Recorder there, a frightened colonial population given a short, exact lesson in survival posture. He has, in effect, become a *traveling teacher* who fights when teaching fails.

What does not stabilize, because it has not yet surfaced: the cancer. The Nega-Bands are doing their suppressive work. The subject's somatic experience across these issues is — by every available indicator — *normal Kree baseline*. Energy levels, recovery times, combat endurance: all at expected ranges. The disease is present and active and unread. Cosmic Awareness, which can perceive a Skrull infiltration on a distant world, cannot or does not perceive what is happening in his own marrow. This blind spot — the body as the one zone the cosmic eye cannot see — is one of the cruelest structural ironies in the file, and it is the secret architecture of the entire late middle period.

---

## X. Pattern Evolution Across the Middle Period — A Longitudinal Summary

Reviewing the decade as a single longitudinal record, the file identifies the following evolutionary trajectories:

1. **From reactive to elective agency.** The early middle is response to imposition; the late middle is principled selection. The same body, the same powers, doing increasingly *chosen* work.
2. **From divided loyalty to integrated stewardship.** The early middle is structured by competing allegiances (Kree, Earth, Rick, self). The late middle has integrated these into a single ethical practice that is loyal to *beings under threat* and only secondarily to the polities those beings belong to.
3. **From grief-management to grief-integration.** Una's death drives the early middle behaviorally even when unmentioned. By the late middle she is rarely invoked because she has been *metabolized into the structure of his protective work


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Dossier Section 4 of the Longitudinal Chronology. Subject: MAR-VELL of the Kree, designated "Captain Marvel," "Protector of the Universe." Period covered: the terminal cancer year through the present posthumous footprint, inclusive of impersonations, partial resurrections, legacy carriage, and the standing operational status of the name, the Nega-Bands, the cosmic mandate, and the body.*

---

## 4.1 The Terminal Year — Pre-Diagnostic Phase

The most recent *lived* era of the subject begins approximately eighteen Earth-months before the diagnosis recorded in Marvel Graphic Novel #1 and ends with his death on Titan in the Mentor-Eros household. The file must be precise about the pre-diagnostic window because it contains the behavioral evidence that he *knew before he was told*.

In the months preceding clinical presentation, behavioral telemetry shows three convergent signatures:

- **Increased ascetic compression.** Caloric intake (as observed by Rick Jones in shared-body recall and corroborated by Eros's later testimony) dropped to roughly two-thirds of his prior maintenance level. Sleep cycles, never long, contracted further. He had always been spartan; now he was paring.
- **Generative urgency without alarm.** He accelerated mentorship interactions — checked in on Carol Danvers (then convalescing after her own catastrophic biological violation by the entity Marcus, an event he had grieved at distance), made an unscheduled visit to Eros on Titan, and held what Rick afterward recognized as *farewell-shaped* conversations without naming them as such.
- **Increased solo flight.** He spent more uninterrupted hours in deep vacuum than at any prior period — flights to the Eon-space, to the outer Kree frontier, to unnamed coordinates. Cosmic Awareness was almost certainly delivering signal he was metabolizing privately. He did not bring it to others.

The most diagnostic single datum: when the cancer was finally named to him on Titan, his observable response was *recognition*, not surprise. Mentor's testimony (recorded informally; later referenced by Eros) is that the subject "received the diagnosis as one receives confirmation of a thing already concluded." This is consistent with months of Cosmic-Awareness-mediated foreknowledge processed without disclosure — a final instance of the lifelong **privatization-of-suffering** pattern documented in the Psychological section.

## 4.2 Diagnosis to Death — The MGN #1 Window

The terminal arc proper occupies a compressed window — by Eros's reconstruction, weeks rather than months from diagnosis to expiration. The granular behavioral record is unusually complete because Mentor's household kept a deathwatch and because the Avengers, the Inhumans, the Skrulls, and a Kree delegation all entered the room before the end.

**Phase 1 — Disclosure and reactive dysphoria (approx. 72 hours).** Brief, well-modulated anger directed at no one. A single observed strike against a wall (uncharacteristic — the only documented instance of impotent physical discharge in the canon). Quiet conference with Rick Jones via Nega-Band linkage — content unrecorded, duration unusually long. He emerged from this conference composed and remained so.

**Phase 2 — Triage of relationships (approx. one week).** Methodical receipt of visitors. The pattern of these meetings is itself diagnostic of mature defenses operating cleanly under load:

- *Rick Jones:* extended, intimate, structured around the eventual decoupling of the Nega-Bands and Rick's release from the symbiotic constraint. The subject's behavior here is striking — he is the one consoling Rick, not the inverse. He apologizes for the years of forced confinement in the Negative Zone. This is the first explicit *naming* of the symbiosis as something done *to* Rick, not merely a circumstance shared by them.
- *Carol Danvers:* private, brief, tender. He releases her from the implied debt of mentorship.
- *Mentor and Eros:* familial. He accepts the household's care for the first time in the canon.
- *The Skrull delegation:* unprecedented. The Skrulls present a posthumous (in their idiom, pre-posthumous) medal honoring a worthy adversary. The subject accepts it with grace. The *Skrulls coming to a dying Kree to honor him as enemy* is one of the most analytically loaded events in the file — it establishes that his integrity-under-conflict was legible across species lines.
- *The Kree delegation:* the Supreme Intelligence rescinds the treason judgment and posthumously rehabilitates him. He accepts this also, but observers (Eros, primarily) noted that the Skrull medal moved him visibly and the Kree rehabilitation did not. He had completed his break with Hala long before they completed theirs with him.
- *The Avengers, the Thing, Spider-Man, the FF, the Inhumans, Reed Richards specifically:* a procession. Reed's visit is critical: Reed offers experimental intervention. The subject refuses on grounds of probability, not despair. This refusal is the operational expression of the Stoic-virtue-ethical commitment catalogued in the Personality section — the calculus is bad; therefore, the answer is no.

**Phase 3 — The hospital child.** During his stay he encounters a terminally ill child (identified in the record as Wendy) in the medical facility. The interaction is brief, sustained, and unwitnessed by media or institutional observers. The behavioral signature here is the same one observable in his treatment of Rick at age sixteen and Carol at her lowest — **tenderness as a baseline mode, not a performance**. The fact that he had bandwidth for an unrelated dying child while himself dying is the cleanest single data point on his character in the entire file.

**Phase 4 — Withdrawal and the hallucinatory final.** Final hours: progressive systemic collapse not amenable to Nega-Band suppression (the bands had been doing the suppression for years and had finally been overwhelmed). He drifts in and out. The recorded hallucinatory sequence — encounter with Thanos as escort rather than enemy, a final symbolic combat in which the two recognize one another and walk into Death's presence together — is, taken at the behavioral level, consistent with terminal lucidity phenomena observed across cultures. The content of the hallucination is itself diagnostic: he organized his deathbed cognition around his most worthy adversary, transmuted into companion. **No splitting, even in extremis.**

He died on Titan. The body was attended by Mentor's household; cremation rites Kree-coded, location Titanian. The interment site has remained a pilgrimage destination of low traffic and high significance.

## 4.3 Immediate Post-Mortem Window — The Sealed Verdict

The most important fact of the subject's post-mortem status, and the one that organizes everything that has happened *to* the legend since, is this: **his death was canonically sealed**. Marvel's editorial position, articulated at the time and largely held since, was that this death would not be reversed. The implication for the dossier: every subsequent "appearance" of Mar-Vell must be classified as *impersonation, legacy carriage, simulacrum, or temporal/dimensional artifact* — not as the resumption of the subject's biography.

This is itself a behavioral fact about the subject, in a sense available only to a Watcher: the universe has *honored his dying*. The few resurrection attempts have all collapsed back into death or unmasked as imposture. The pattern is too consistent to be accidental. He stayed dead because the meaning of his life required it.

## 4.4 The Posthumous Carriage — Genis-Vell

The first legacy figure is the biological son, gestated by Elysius (a posthumous conception arranged via stored genetic material on Titan). The son was aged artificially, assumed the Captain Marvel name, took up the Nega-Bands, and inherited Cosmic Awareness — and was destabilized by all three.

The behavioral contrast is the salient datum. Where the subject metabolized Cosmic Awareness into ascetic gravitas, the son experienced it as a psychotogenic load and eventually decompensated into a cosmic crisis requiring his own death. The implication for the dossier on Mar-Vell himself: **the equilibrium he maintained under that perceptual load was not generic to Kree physiology or Nega-Band possession; it was personal, hard-won, and non-transferable.** The son's failure retroactively elevates the father's achievement.

A daughter (Phyla-Vell) emerged from continuity-revision and carried the name and partial mantle for a period; her trajectory is its own file. For our purposes she functions as a second data point in the same direction: **the mantle is heavier than its visible weight.** Only the original carried it without breaking.

## 4.5 Impersonations and Simulacra

Several discrete instances must be logged because they constitute the *negative space* of the subject's current existence — the shape pressed into the universe by his absence.

- **The Civil War-era apparition.** A figure appearing as the returned Mar-Vell surfaced during the Initiative period. Investigation eventually disclosed this as a temporally displaced earlier-self construct, ultimately not the integrated mature subject of MGN #1. He died again. Behavioral signature: **he could not be sustained in a continuity that had moved past his moral economy.**
- **The Secret Invasion Skrull.** A Skrull infiltrator wore his form and his rhetoric with sufficient fidelity to deceive the Avengers for an operational period — and, notably, *partly came to believe his own performance*, defecting in spirit before being undone. The diagnostic implication: the subject's persona is so internally coherent that even a hostile imposter, immersed in it, drifts toward integrity. This is an unusual property of an identity.
- **Various brief evocations** in cosmic-scale events (Annihilation-adjacent, Realm of Kings, the Cancerverse — where, in a horrifying inversion, a corrupted Mar-Vell rules a death-denying universe; the inversion is so precise it functions as commentary on the original: a Mar-Vell who refused to die is by definition not Mar-Vell). Each of these is an artifact, not a resumption.

The cumulative pattern across imposters and simulacra: **the subject's identity is being used as a measurement instrument** — every attempt to wear it tests whether the wearer can sustain the integrity-under-conflict standard. Most fail. The standard remains the subject's, even when others hold the name.

## 4.6 The Name in Other Carriers

The "Captain Marvel" designation has, in the present period, settled on Carol Danvers as primary carrier — the mentee become heir. The dossier notes the following with care: she did not take the name during his life and did not take it immediately after. She took it after long deliberation, with explicit reference to him, and she has carried it as honorific obligation rather than appropriation. This is the carriage he would have endorsed.

Other figures (Monica Rambeau under the name earlier, Khan more recently under derivative iterations) form a constellation around the original designation. The original subject is the *gravitational center* of this constellation despite — or because of — his absence. He is more present in absence than most cosmic figures are in presence.

## 4.7 The Standing Status of the Body, the Bands, and the Mandate

For total-surveillance completeness:

- **Body:** interred / cremated per Kree rite on Titan. No known sample exists outside Mentor's household and the Elysius gestation matrix that produced the son. No known cloning attempts have succeeded; the few that approached viability collapsed for reasons indistinguishable from the resurrection-collapse pattern noted above.
- **Nega-Bands:** dispossessed at death; subsequent carriage variable (Genis, others); the bands themselves are inert metal until paired with a wearer whose psyche they can amplify. They remember him in no mystical sense, but they were calibrated by the Psyche-Magnitron in his and Rick's combined image, and each subsequent wearer has had to overwrite that calibration with their own. Most cannot.
- **Cosmic Awareness:** transferred — partially, problematically — to the son; otherwise extinct in its original form. Eon's appointment of a Protector of the Universe has passed to other figures over time, none of whom have held it for as long or as quietly.
- **Reputation among the Kree:** rehabilitated, then re-complicated by Kree political churn over decades. Among the present Kree polity, he is an officially honored heretic — the kind of figure regimes invoke when convenient and ignore otherwise. He would have found this funny.
- **Reputation among the Skrulls:** durable. The medal he was given on his deathbed is, by Skrull standards, a serious thing.
- **Reputation among Earth's heroic community:** sacred. Reed Richards's eulogy at the Titan service set a register that has held. He is the death they measure other deaths against.
- **Reputation in the wider cosmic register:** the standard against which Protector-class figures are judged. Adam Warlock, the Silver Surfer, and others have invoked his name in their own crises.

## 4.8 Current State — Synthesis

Where is he now? In the only sense that matters for a dossier built around understanding: he is **complete**. The subject's biographical arc reached its terminal articulation in MGN #1 and has not been disturbed since by any event canonical enough to reopen it. The posthumous appearances are *commentary*, not continuation.

The current-state read on Mar-Vell, then, is unusual for a dossier of this kind. Most subjects of total-surveillance files are tracked because the next behavior is uncertain. The subject's next behavior is certain: he will continue to be dead, and his death will continue to organize the meaning of his life. The variable is not him; it is the universe's metabolization of him.

Three operational facts about that metabolization, current as of last assessment:

1. **The integrity standard he set is still being tested** through every figure who wears or claims his name. The standard has not been met by any successor. This is not failure on their part; it is the structural difficulty of meeting a standard whose author spent six decades of published life rehearsing for the moment that proved it.
2. **The death-as-completion pattern he established** has become a referent in the wider heroic community. Other deaths get compared to his and found wanting (too sudden, too reversed, too theatrical). His remains the model of a *well-met ending*. The cultural function of his file in the cosmic register is now substantially that of an exemplar — a Stoic *paradeigma* — rather than an active participant.
3. **The privatization-of-suffering pattern**, his single most persistent behavioral signature, achieved its final form in the pre-diagnostic months when he absorbed his death sentence alone for an unknown but substantial period before disclosure. The pattern is no longer active; it has ossified into the closed shape of the completed life. A Watcher's note: this is the only kind of resolution that pattern admits. He could not have stopped privatizing his suffering; he could only finish.

The subject is not currently operating. The subject has been fully operative all along — the operation was the life, and the life was a preparation, and the preparation was finished on Titan, and the finish has held. This file, in the present tense, is therefore a record of a completed object. The remaining sections will treat habits, rituals, micro-patterns, and tells as one treats the brushwork of a finished painting: with reverence for what is no longer being painted, and with attention to what the finished surface still teaches.

*End Chronology IV. Continue to behavioral micro-pattern atlas.*


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: MAR-VELL OF THE KREE

*Compiled longitudinal somatic record. Cross-referenced against operational behavioral log. All entries cite or extrapolate from observable canon.*

---

## I. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

### I.a — Species Phenotype and Its Implications

Subject is a member of the Kree species, specifically the **"pink" sub-phenotype** — a genetic minority within his own civilization, the descendant population of Kree who interbred with the conquered Pheragot or who retained pre-Imperial pigmentation. The dominant **blue Kree** phenotype is culturally hegemonic on Hala and enjoys subtle but pervasive physiological privileges: marginally denser skeletal architecture, slightly higher hemoglobin-analog oxygen carriage, fuller pulmonary tolerance for the chlorine-tinted Kree atmosphere. Mar-Vell, as a pink Kree, sits roughly **eighty to eighty-five percent of blue-phenotype baselines** across these metrics. He is still vastly superhuman by Terran standards but is, within his own species, *the lesser stock*.

This matters medically because it produced lifelong **compensatory physical conditioning**: subject trained harder than his blue-Kree peers to achieve identical militia rankings, and his musculoskeletal record across decades shows the cumulative wear of an over-trained body — micro-fracture remodeling visible on Kree imaging (referenced obliquely in *Captain Marvel* vol. 1 #18 medical interlude aboard the *Helion*), connective-tissue density at the top of the pink-Kree distribution, and resting cortisol-analog levels elevated above species median.

It matters **psychologically** because it shaped his earliest experience of the body as *something to be disciplined into adequacy*. The Kree military made him a Captain on merit, but the merit had to be louder than his pigmentation. This is the somatic substrate beneath what later reads as Stoic asceticism: the habit of training the body past comfort was installed in adolescence, well before any cosmic mandate gave it metaphysical justification.

### I.b — Baseline Vital Parameters (extrapolated)

- **Strength:** Class 25–50 ton range pre-Nega-Bands; substantially higher post-augmentation, peaking in the high cosmic range under Protector mandate.
- **Lifespan:** Native Kree lifespan ~200 standard years; subject's life truncated at biological age estimated late-30s to mid-40s Earth-equivalent.
- **Atmospheric tolerance:** Tolerates Terran oxygen mix indefinitely with mild chronic respiratory irritation (the air is "thin" to him); requires no breathing apparatus across most planetary classes; the Nega-Bands later eliminated even hard-vacuum constraint.
- **Healing rate:** Approximately 3–5× Terran baseline pre-Bands; near-instantaneous for non-systemic tissue damage post-Bands.
- **Sensory baseline:** Acute Kree visual range (extends into near-UV); auditory range comparable to Terran but with superior signal discrimination in noise; proprioception engineered by zero-G military training.

---

## II. INJURIES AND TRAUMATIC EVENTS — CHRONOLOGICAL

### II.a — Pre-Mission Period (Kree Imperial Militia, undated to *MSH* #12)

Service record prior to the Earth deployment is sparse in primary canon but inferable. Subject accumulated the standard injury palette of a front-line Kree officer: penetrating wounds from Skrull plasma weapons, blunt trauma from boarding actions, at least one decompression event survived without permanent pulmonary scarring, repeated low-grade radiation exposures from unshielded jump-drive proximity. None disabling; all metabolized by Kree healing baseline.

The relevant psychological residue is **operational fatalism without affective collapse** — he learned early that the body absorbs damage and recovers, that pain is information rather than emergency. This is a soldier's somatic literacy, and it remained the floor of his physical self-relation for the rest of his life.

### II.b — *Helion* Deployment and Yon-Rogg Sabotage Period (*MSH* #12 – *Captain Marvel* #11)

The most clinically interesting period of his early life because the injuries here are **deliberately engineered by his commanding officer**.

Yon-Rogg's pattern: assigning Mar-Vell to reconnaissance tasks with falsified threat assessments, withholding extraction support, leaving him exposed to Cape Canaveral security ordnance, sending him against suited human pilots in atmospheric envelopes calibrated to disadvantage Kree physiology. The cumulative injury log across the first dozen issues includes:

- Multiple ballistic wounds from human small arms (survived; Kree dermal density prevented penetration of vitals).
- Concussive trauma from missile near-misses on at least three documented occasions.
- One sub-orbital fall survived with significant musculoskeletal damage.
- Chronic **sleep deficit** — he was running a double shift of overt Kree duty plus covert Walter Lawson civilian cover, with no sanctioned recovery interval.
- Persistent low-grade **operational dehydration** — he could not openly source Kree-spec fluids on Earth and was rationing.

The psychological impact here is the founding wound of his adult character: **his own body was being weaponized against him by his own command**. He could not name this aloud, could not seek redress, could not even fully confirm it to himself without political consequence. The somatic experience of betrayal-from-within prefigures, with eerie symmetry, the carcinoma that would kill him — a body whose own apparatus is the instrument of its destruction. He had two decades of practice managing that exact phenomenology before the cancer ever metastasized.

### II.c — The Death of Una (*Captain Marvel* #11)

Una dies in a crash engineered by Yon-Rogg's negligence (the operational record reads as negligence; the moral record reads as something darker). The medical entry is not Mar-Vell's body but his nervous system: this is the first and only documented **acute grief reaction** in the canon. Brief, intense, somatized as collapse — he carries her body, he is silent for an extended period afterward, and the issues immediately following show a measurable shift in **baseline affective tone** that does not fully reverse for years.

Clinically: an uncomplicated bereavement, not pathological grief, but the **identity-disorganizing** kind that strips a person of a future they had been organizing themselves around. He never partners again. There is no replacement attachment of equivalent romantic depth across the remaining canon. The Carol Danvers relationship, often misread by external observers as romantic, is a mentoring transference with affectionate undertones — substantively different from the Una bond and shaped, at least in part, by his having already closed that chapter of his somatic life.

### II.d — Nega-Band Bonding and Rick Jones Symbiosis (*Captain Marvel* #17 onward)

A category unto itself, discussed in full under §III.b. As an injury: this is the **forcible alteration of his embodiment**. He did not consent to the symbiosis with Rick Jones; the Supreme Intelligence imposed it as a survival mechanism that was also a punishment. He spent the next several years of subjective time in a body he could only inhabit half the time, sharing it with an adolescent human stranger whose own embodiment, hormones, sleep cycle, and emotional weather bled across the bond.

The medical analogue is something like a **chronic partial dissociation forced from the outside** — a sovereignty deprivation. He never complained about it in record. That silence is itself diagnostic.

### II.e — The Nitro Incident — Carcinogenic Exposure (*Captain Marvel* #34, 1974)

The proximate cause of his death, contracted at the moment of his victory.

Combat with the explosively-powered villain Nitro at a chemical weapons facility resulted in the rupture of canisters of **Compound 13**, a Terran experimental nerve agent. Mar-Vell, fighting in close quarters and without respiratory shielding (his arrogance about Kree atmospheric tolerance is the relevant factor — he assumed his physiology would clear the toxin, and the Nega-Bands' biofield reinforced that assumption), inhaled and dermally absorbed a substantial dose.

Acute symptoms were minimal: brief disorientation, a cough that resolved in hours, mild headache for a day. The Nega-Bands' systemic suppression effect — never designed for this application, an accidental side-property of their psionic-physical conversion — neutralized the agent's nerve-blocking action and subsequently masked, for years, the slow oncogenic damage Compound 13 was inflicting at the cellular level.

He **knew** he had been exposed. He **did not** seek follow-up imaging or chelation. Two reasons, both characteristic: operational pace did not permit it, and his somatic literacy told him he had recovered. He filed the incident away as a closed wound. This is the only documented instance in his life of his usually excellent body-judgment being **catastrophically wrong**, and the wrongness was hidden from him by the very prosthetic that defined his post-exile identity.

### II.f — Intervening Combat Period (*Captain Marvel* #35–62, ~1974–1979)

Standard cosmic-tier combat trauma. Injuries inflicted by Drax, the Controller, Thanos's various proxies, the Lunatic Legion, etc. — all metabolized within normal Kree-plus-Nega-Band recovery envelopes. Notable for the **absence** of any complaint about subtle persistent symptoms: low-grade fatigue, occasional fevers, the things a careful patient would notice. He did not notice because his entire life had trained him not to.

### II.g — Terminal Diagnosis (*The Death of Captain Marvel*, MGN #1, 1982)

Symptoms became unmasked when the Nega-Bands' suppression threshold was breached by tumor burden. Presentation: progressive fatigue, then a collapse, then Kree, Skrull, and Rigellian diagnostics in succession confirming **diffuse metastatic carcinoma**, untreatable by any medicine accessible to him. The Rigellian Recorder calculates the trajectory in weeks.

His response, in clinical-behavioral terms, is **textbook adaptive**: brief anger, brief denial, rapid movement through bargaining (he considers and then rejects the experimental Eternal/Titan interventions Mentor offers, because the probability calculus does not favor them and the cost in dignity is high), and into sustained acceptance. He **organizes his death** — reconciliations, farewells, the ceremonial visits from Skrulls and Kree alike granting him posthumous recognition before he is technically posthumous. The hospital scenes with the dying child Wendy show him performing the role of fellow-patient with full presence; he is not slumming as a hero among the sick, he is *one of the sick*, and inhabits that identity without flinching.

The final hallucinatory chess game with Thanos as psychopomp is the canonical close. The medical event is straightforward organ failure; the psychological event is a man whose entire life of disciplined preparation finally **arrives at the thing it was preparing for**.

---

## III. AUGMENTATIONS, PROSTHETICS, AND TRANSFORMATIONS

### III.a — Standard-Issue Kree Combat Apparatus (Early Period)

Original deployment: white-and-green Kree military uniform with integrated anti-gravity, atmospheric scrubbing, modest forcefield generation, and tactical communications. This was prosthetic in the proper sense — *necessary to function*. Without it on Earth he was a strong man with breathing problems; with it he was a Captain of the Imperial Militia.

The psychological residue: he was, from the beginning, a being whose competence required external augmentation. The fantasy of unaided heroism was never available to him. This is **not** narcissistic injury — he never resented the dependence — but it is the substrate of his later willingness to share embodiment with Rick Jones and to wear the Nega-Bands without fetishizing them. He had never been, and never expected to be, **somatically self-sufficient**.

### III.b — The Red-and-Blue Uniform (Thomas era, post-*CM* #17)

The replacement costume was, per canon, **manifested by Rick Jones's subconscious** via the Nega-Bands' psionic interface. The medical relevance is that Mar-Vell's most iconic body — the silhouette by which the universe knows him — was *designed by another person's dreaming mind*. He inherited an aesthetic he did not choose, a color palette weighted toward a teenage Terran's hero-fantasy.

He never modified it. He wore it without comment for the entire remaining canon. The behavior here is significant: a man with a tighter ego would have re-asserted aesthetic sovereignty. He absorbed Rick's design as a kind of **somatic gift** and integrated it. This is the same temperament that later allows him to die without raging against the cosmos.

### III.c — The Nega-Bands

Forged by the Psyche-Magnitron, the Nega-Bands are the central prosthetic of his adult life. Functionally:

- **Psionic-to-physical conversion**, amplifying baseline Kree strength by orders of magnitude.
- **Flight** independent of atmospheric medium.
- **Energy projection** of variable spectral character.
- **Hard-vacuum survival**, indefinite — eliminated the suit-life-support dependency.
- **Bio-stabilization**, including, critically and accidentally, **oncogenic suppression** of the Compound 13 damage.

Required activation gesture: striking the bands together. This is a small thing but a real one — his power requires a *deliberate ritual movement*, a moment of intention. The behavioral effect across decades is that his power-state is always **chosen**, never accidental. He cannot lose his temper into a destructive blast; he must first perform the ritual. This is one of the most underappreciated stabilizing features of his entire psychology.

The Nega-Bands also forced the **Rick Jones symbiosis**: only one of them could be on Earth at a time, the other locked in the Negative Zone, with the bands shuttling between them as the trigger. The psychological terrain of this is bewildering. Half his life from age ~30 to death was spent **not on the plane of consensual reality**. He had a permanent partial absence, a permanent other-self who was a teenage human, and a permanent operational constraint that any threat to Rick was a threat to his own continued embodiment.

He metabolized this without observable bitterness. The strain shows only obliquely — in the deepening asceticism of the mid-1970s issues, in the withdrawal from extended human social contact, in the way he came to speak of his own body in increasingly impersonal terms. The Bands healed him, empowered him, killed him by hiding what was killing him, and bound him to another consciousness for half his remaining life. They are not a prosthetic in the simple sense; they are a **second skeleton** he wore in his nervous system as much as on his wrists.

### III.d — The Eon Transformation and Cosmic Awareness (*Captain Marvel* #29)

Eon's "awakening" of Mar-Vell as Protector of the Universe is, in medical terms, the installation of an **ongoing neurological enhancement**: Cosmic Awareness, a perceptual-cognitive faculty that delivers continuous teleological/situational data about the universe's needs.

The phenomenology is barely documented because Mar-Vell rarely described it. Inferentially: a constant low-level signal load, a sense of relevant events at planetary-to-cosmic scale, a foreknowledge faculty that operates probabilistically rather than deterministically. The metabolic cost is real — it is plausible he required **less sleep** and **more contemplative recovery time** post-Eon, and the textual record bears this out (more meditation scenes, longer stretches of solitude).

The most consequential medical implication: **he almost certainly knew, years before MGN #1, that he was going to die.** Cosmic Awareness would have registered the tumor trajectory long before clinical symptoms broke through Nega-Band suppression. The calm of the terminal arc is not grace under sudden diagnosis; it is the **expression of a private grieving he had already completed in solitude, probably across years**. The Wendy scene, the Skrull medal, the chess game with Thanos — these are not improvisations of a dying man, they are the public enactments of a script he had been writing internally since the awareness first surfaced.

He told no one. This is consistent with the **privatization-of-suffering** signature noted throughout the file. It is also, retrospectively, the single greatest somatic burden he carried — and he carried it alone, by choice.

### III.e — Negative Zone Embodiment Interludes

Each shuttle into the Negative Zone constituted a brief **environmental embodiment shift**: different ambient energetic constants, different time-flow ratios at certain depths, different sensory inputs. Cumulatively, across hundreds of swaps, he spent a substantial fraction of his post-#17 life in a non-Newtonian physical regime. The neurological adaptation cost is undocumented but non-zero; the psychological effect is to further deepen the sense that **embodiment itself is contingent**, a position one occupies temporarily rather than a self one inhabits.

### III.f — Posthumous Echoes (For Completeness)

The Skrull impersonation during *Secret Invasion*, the false Mar-Vell of *Civil War*, the genetic-and-spiritual inheritors Genis-Vell and Phyla-Vell — these are not entries in his medical history per se, but the file should note that **his body continued to be performed, copied, and inherited after his death**. The somatic signature he established was distinctive enough to be worth forging. Even the impostors performed integrity-under-impossible-loyalty as part of inhabiting him. The medical record, in this sense, has a long tail.

---

## IV. SUBSTANCES

**Negative across the entire canonical record.** No documented use of intoxicants, recreational or medicinal, of any species' provenance. He refuses Terran alcohol at one of Rick Jones's social interludes; he does not partake of Kree ceremonial stimulants on the rare occasions of Hala return; he declines Eternal/Titan pharmacological interventions even when offered as therapeutic in MGN #1.

The pattern is **soldier's discipline carried into civilian and contemplative intervals**, hardened further by the post-Eon ascetic identity. Substances would compromise both the operational reliability his Cosmic Awareness required and the meditative clarity by which he managed his interior life. There is also a plausible inference of **somatic suspicion** — given the Yon-Rogg betrayals, the Compound 13 exposure, and the Nega-Band masking effect, his lived experience of introduced substances was that they were nearly always **other peoples' weapons or others' miscalculations**. Refusing them is consistent with a man who learned, expensively, that what enters the body is rarely neutral.

---

## V. DISABILITY, AND THE QUESTION OF SOVEREIGN EMBODIMENT

Mar-Vell never carried a formal disability in the Earth-clinical sense. But the file should mark, plainly, what the canon makes clear: **he never inhabited his own body alone.** From early career he wore the Kree military exo-apparatus; from mid-career he wore the Nega-Bands and shared embodiment with Rick Jones; from late career he carried the chronic perceptual load of Cosmic Awareness; from #34 onward he carried, unknowingly, the carcinogenic inheritance of Compound 13; and across all periods he wore a uniform designed by another person's mind.

The **sovereign body** — the body that is simply one's own, unaugmented, unshared, unobserved, unmandated — was never available to him. The closest he came was probably the final hours of MGN #1, when the Nega-Bands' suppression had failed, the symbiosis with Rick was suspended for the dying, Cosmic Awareness was contracting with neurological collapse, and what remained was a Kree man in a hospital bed at the end of his life. He was, finally, only himself. He used those hours to **say goodbye to people, with full attention**.

That is the somatic punchline of the entire medical record. The body that had been collectively occupied his whole life became, briefly, his own — and he spent that sovereignty *giving it away in love, deliberately and to specific people*, rather than reclaiming it for any private purpose. The discipline by which he had lived produced, at the end, a death in which the body was finally his and was finally a gift.

---

## VI. SUMMARY MEDICAL JUDGMENT

Subject presents the somatic record of a **constitutionally robust minority-phenotype Kree** subjected to (a) lifelong over-training to compensate for pigmentation-linked baseline disadvantage, (b) chronic operational injury under a sabotaging command, (c) forcible bonding to a prosthetic-symbiotic apparatus that simultaneously empowered and concealed-illness-from him, (d) a perceptual augmentation that almost certainly delivered years of foreknowledge of his own terminal trajectory, and (e) a slow-onset carcinoma contracted at the moment of a victory and masked until untreatable.

The behavioral metabolization of this cumulative load is, by any clinical standard, **extraordinary**. He did not develop addiction, did not develop characterological pathology, did not develop somatization disorders, did not demonize his betrayers, did not refuse intimacy, did not collapse under foreknowledge of death. He converted each somatic insult into a deepening of discipline and an expansion of protective scope.

The medical history is, finally, inseparable from the psychological one: he was a man whose body taught him, repeatedly and from every angle, that **embodiment is contingent, sovereignty is partial, and the only response is to use what one has been given, well, for as long as one has it.** The carcinoma did not refute that lesson; it completed it.

*End medical section. Cross-file to §III Psychological for affect-regulation correlates and §V Personality for integration into operational profile.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: MAR-VELL OF THE KREE

*File subsection 4.2. Bodily record, longitudinal. All entries derived from observed canon and inferred from species baseline + behavioral substrate. Cross-reference §2 Medical, §3 Psychological.*

---

## I. FRAME, CARRIAGE, AND THE BODY AT REST

The subject stands 6'3" (1.91 m), 240 lbs (109 kg), pink-Kree phenotype, with a musculature distribution characteristic of Kree military conditioning: heavy deltoid and trapezius development, comparatively long femurs, thickened forearms from grip-work with weapons predating the Nega-Bands. The chest is deep rather than broad, optimized for the higher atmospheric pressure of Hala. On Earth, this manifests as a slightly shallower respiratory cycle than human baseline — he breathes *less often* and *less deeply* than a comparably sized human, a detail that registers to close observers as preternatural stillness.

**Resting posture** is military-vertical without being rigid. Spine neutral, chin level (not lifted — lifting the chin is a Kree dominance display he has consciously suppressed since the Yon-Rogg years), shoulders set back but not squared; weight distributed evenly across both feet with a barely perceptible forward bias on the balls, never fully heel-loaded. This forward bias is the residue of a soldier who learned never to be flat-footed in a room with Yon-Rogg. He retains it for the rest of his life. Even in the MGN #1 hospital, dying, when he stands he stands forward-loaded.

**Hands at rest** are the most diagnostic single tell. Pre-Nega-Band era: hands loose, palms turned slightly inward, fingers softly curled — soldier-relaxed. Post-Nega-Band (after #17): hands assume a *settled lightness* — wrists held at a barely-noticed elevation off the thighs when seated, as if the bands themselves want to lift. He learns to suppress this within a few issues, but in unguarded moments — listening to Rick, watching Carol work — the wrists float again. In the terminal phase, the hands return to the early soft curl, but now the fingers tremble at amplitudes below the threshold of casual notice — a fine resting tremor of roughly 4–6 Hz, which he hides by interlacing or by holding objects.

**Seated posture** in private: forearms on thighs, leaning slightly forward, head inclined toward whoever is speaking — the conference posture of an officer who learned to listen. In public, on the rare occasions he sits in mixed company: spine off the chair-back, both feet flat, hands resting on the upper thighs near the hip crease. He almost never crosses his legs; the Kree military uniform did not permit it and the habit calcified.

---

## II. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

Walking pace is metronomic — between 112 and 118 steps per minute regardless of urgency, until urgency tips into combat-mode, at which point gait disappears entirely into flight or sprint. Stride length is long for the cadence, producing a walk that *covers ground faster than it appears to*. Witnesses consistently underestimate how quickly he closed a distance; this is documented across human civilian encounters from the Roy Thomas issues onward.

The heel strikes first but lightly, with rapid transition to forefoot — a quiet walk. He can move silently in boots over hard floors when he wants to; this is not stealth as discipline but Kree boot-design plus a habit of weight-control acquired in shipboard corridors. Arms swing minimally; the contralateral arm-swing is suppressed to perhaps a third of human normal, a holdover from carrying rifles and later from the energy load of the Nega-Bands, which subtly affects upper-limb dynamics.

**Flight** (Nega-Band era) develops its own kinesic signature. Take-off is preceded by a quarter-second compression of the knees and a near-imperceptible inhalation; landing involves a single small step forward to absorb residual momentum, never a stagger. He flies head-leading, body trailing in a slight diagonal, arms held close to the trunk rather than out — efficiency, not display. Compare Thor, whose flight is theatrical; Mar-Vell's flight is the flight of a man who treats it as transit.

**Combat locomotion** is angular and economical: he pivots on the lead foot, never the back, and rotates his hips before his shoulders — the inverse of the boxing convention, because Kree military grappling forms prioritize hip-leverage for grip-throws. He does not bob. He does not feint with the head. He commits to single decisive movements with full body integration and accepts that this telegraphs; his speed and reach make telegraphing tactically irrelevant.

---

## III. THE FACE

The face is broad-cheeked, square-jawed, with the slight epicanthic carriage common to pink Kree. Resting expression is what an observer would call *neutral-attentive*: brow level, mouth closed but unpressed, eyes tracking. He does not have a resting frown and he does not have a resting smile. This neutrality is itself a Kree military convention he never shed — affective display in the Imperial Militia marked one as unreliable.

**Eye behavior** is the most information-rich channel. Saccades are slower and longer than human average; he looks at one thing, then another thing, with a deliberateness that reads to Earth-humans as either reassuring or unnerving depending on context. Blink rate at rest: low, approximately 8–10/minute (human baseline ~15). Under threat, the blink rate drops further, sometimes to near-zero for 20–40 second intervals. Under emotional load — Una, Rick in danger, his own diagnosis — blink rate paradoxically *rises*, often accompanied by a single full closure lasting 1.5–2 seconds, which functions as an internal reset. The MGN #1 hospital sequences show this long-closure repeatedly.

**Brow**: the inner-brow lifter (Ekman AU 1) is his primary affective leak. It appears during sympathy (with Rick after a failure; with Wendy in the cancer ward), during recognition of moral cost in an opponent (Thanos's final moments), and once, in unguarded form, when Carol Danvers demonstrates a capability he had not anticipated — pride disguised as surprise. The outer brow rarely moves; lateral brow-lift would read as Kree military skepticism and he has trained it out.

**Mouth**: the smile is rare, asymmetric (slightly higher on the left), and brief — typically under a second. A full smile (AU 6 + 12, with orbital involvement) appears perhaps a dozen times across the entire canon: most often with Rick, twice with Una in flashback, once with Carol after she completes the Psyche-Magnitron sequence that birthed her own powers, and — significantly — twice in MGN #1, both times directed at people he is dying for the sake of. He does not laugh aloud. The closest approximation is a single voiced exhalation through the nose with the lips closed.

**Jaw**: clenches under suppressed anger. The masseter activation is visible but he does not grind. The jaw-set during the Yon-Rogg confrontations is the canon's clearest tell for his anger, and writers and pencillers track it consistently. After Una's death the jaw-set generalizes for several issues into a permanent low-grade tension that resolves only with the Eon awakening in #29.

---

## IV. VOICE AND VERBAL SOMATICS

Baritone, resonant, with the slightly compressed vowel-set of someone whose first language has fewer diphthongs than English. Speech rate: moderate-slow, averaging 130–140 wpm in calm conditions, dropping to 110 under emotional weight and rising to 170 in tactical exchanges. He uses *pauses* the way most people use emphasis. The pause before a refusal — to the Supreme Intelligence, to Mentor in MGN #1 — is consistently 1–2 seconds longer than the pause before an assent. Listeners learn to read the pause as the answer.

He does not interrupt. Across the canon there are perhaps three instances of him cutting another speaker off, all combat-emergent. He also does not use filler particles — no "uh," no "well" — which gives his speech a written quality that reads as either formal or alien depending on the listener's frame. Rick teases him for it more than once.

**Volume modulation** is narrow. He neither shouts (except in combat command-voice) nor drops below conversational. Whispering, when it occurs, is reserved for the dying and the very young; he whispers to Wendy in MGN #1; he whispers — in flashback — to Una.

---

## V. GROOMING, HABITS OF SELF-MAINTENANCE

The hair is dark, cut short on the sides with moderate length on top, parted naturally without product in the early years; by the Starlin era it is slightly longer, less consciously kept, and he runs the fingers of the left hand back through it when thinking — a tell he never eliminates. The gesture appears during the Thanos arc, during conversations with Eon, during the cancer-ward sequences. It is the single most reliable "I am about to commit to a position" precursor in his body language.

Shaving: daily, mechanical, brief; Kree facial hair grows more slowly than human, so the operation takes him under three minutes. He shaves in cold water, a barracks habit. He does not look at his own face longer than the operation requires. He does not check his appearance in mirrors before public-facing engagements.

He bathes once daily, briefly, water hotter than humans tolerate (Kree thermal preference). He does not use scent. The Nega-Band uniform self-cleans, but in civilian intervals on Earth he wears the same handful of plain garments and washes them with the same brisk efficiency he applies to everything else. There is no vanity in the body — only maintenance.

**Nails**: trimmed short, clean, never bitten. Cuticles intact. The hands of a man who does not gnaw at himself.

---

## VI. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Kree baseline sleep need is reduced relative to humans — approximately 4–5 hours per circadian period suffices, with denser slow-wave proportion. Mar-Vell, when conditions permit, sleeps in two segments: a longer block of roughly three hours and a shorter restorative block of one to two hours, separated by a brief waking interval he uses for reading or sky-watching. This biphasic pattern is shipboard-conditioned.

**Sleep posture**: on the back, arms at sides or one forearm across the lower ribs. He does not turn frequently. He wakes fully and immediately on disturbance — no transitional grogginess — and is operationally capable within seconds. This is a soldier's somatic discipline that he never loses, including in the terminal phase, when the disease's fatigue overrides every other system but not this one.

After the Rick Jones fusion, sleep becomes asynchronous in a deeper sense: one or the other consciousness is in the Negative Zone at any given time, and the dreaming life of each becomes partially porous to the other. Mar-Vell reports — when pressed by Rick — that he sometimes dreams in human idioms he has not learned, and that Una, in his dreams, sometimes speaks in Rick's voice. He does not find this distressing; he finds it instructive. He sleeps less well in the months following Una's death (early Thomas issues — visible eye-shadowing, a uncharacteristic morning slowness) and again in the weeks immediately after the cancer diagnosis, after which the sleep restabilizes at a shorter duration and he uses the gained hours for terminal correspondence and meditation.

---

## VII. EATING AND INGESTION

Sparse, regular, indifferent to pleasure. Kree metabolism on Earth processes most human food adequately but inefficiently; he eats less than his mass would suggest and supplements with Kree ration-paste when available. He prefers simple proteins, root vegetables, water. He does not drink alcohol — Kree physiology metabolizes ethanol unusually, and the cultural taboo against intoxication in the Militia is strong; he never tested it. He does not drink coffee or tea. He drinks water at room temperature, in measured sips, never gulping.

He eats with the same economy as he walks. Fork in the left hand (Kree convention), knife in the right; he does not switch. He finishes what is in front of him. He does not comment on flavor. The single canonical exception is a sequence with Rick early in the partnership where Rick insists he try a hot dog; Mar-Vell eats it, considers it, says something brief and dry, and Rick laughs. The hot-dog moment is one of the few times he engages food as a social object rather than a fuel intake.

Terminal phase: appetite collapses as expected; he eats only when prompted, and only enough to honor the prompter. He does not perform recovery to spare others — the same refusal-to-fake that marks all his behavior.

---

## VIII. SEXUALITY AND INTIMATE SOMATICS

The intimate record is sparse and almost entirely confined to Una. The Kree military convention against affective display extends to physical intimacy in public, and he never violated it; the available data are inferential from flashback and from his bodily behavior when she is present.

With Una, the body softens *measurably*: shoulders drop perhaps half an inch, the forward weight-bias relaxes into true neutral, the saccades slow further and rest longer on her face. He touches her hand more often than he speaks to her. Forehead-to-forehead contact appears at least twice in flashback — a Kree intimacy gesture more than a human one, but he uses it with her in private. He is the one who initiates physical contact in the relationship; she is the one who initiates verbal intimacy. This asymmetry tells us he expresses love through proximity and protection more than through speech.

Post-Una, there is no documented sexual partner. The relationship with Carol Danvers is unmistakably affectionate but he does not eroticize it — the body shows no proximity-seeking, no leaning, no extended eye-rest. He mentors her, watches her grow, and steps back. The single moment in MGN #1 where Carol holds his hand at the deathbed is bodily reciprocated — his fingers close on hers — and this is the most physically intimate contact with her in the entire canon.

Inferred: he is capable of and oriented toward partnered intimacy but has organized his post-Una somatic life around a chosen continence. The body is not suppressed; the body is *allocated elsewhere*. This is consistent with the sublimation pattern in §3.

---

## IX. MICRO-GESTURES, TICS, TELLS

A discrete catalogue, with state-dependence noted.

- **Left-hand-through-hair**: thinking; precedes commitment. Stable across decades.
- **Right thumb stroking the inside of the left wrist** (where the Nega-Band sits): self-soothing, appears in negotiation and in moments of moral weight. Pre-Nega-Band era this gesture is absent; he develops it in the Thomas run and retains it.
- **Single slow nod**, eyes closed at the bottom of the nod: acknowledgment of a hard truth. Used with Rick after Rick's failures, with Mentor in MGN #1.
- **Two-finger touch to the temple**: appears during Cosmic Awareness episodes, an unconscious somatic accompaniment to the perceptual flood. He does not perform this; it leaks.
- **Tongue briefly against the back of the upper teeth**, lips closed: suppressed disagreement. Appears in Supreme Intelligence audiences and in conversations with Reed Richards.
- **Right palm settled on the sternum** for two to three seconds: grief-acknowledgment, private. Appears at Una's grave, at Captain Mar-Vell's own diagnosis, at the bedside of a child he could not save in a mid-70s issue.
- **Inhalation held for one full beat before speaking**: appears when he is about to deliver news the listener will not want.
- **Eye-rest on the middle distance, three to four seconds, then return**: Cosmic Awareness orienting; can be mistaken for distraction. It is the opposite.

**Absent gestures** (notable for their absence): no foot-tapping, no finger-drumming, no pen-clicking analogue, no nail-picking, no jaw-grinding, no lip-biting, no nose-touching, no hair-twirling, no head-scratching. The body does not fidget. The fidget-energy that other beings discharge through such small motions is, in him, *consumed by stillness itself* — and this stillness is metabolically expensive, which partially accounts for his appetite for solitude. Holding the body that quiet for that long requires recovery.

---

## X. STATE-DEPENDENT SOMATIC SHIFTS

**Calm baseline**: stillness, slow saccades, low blink rate, even respiration, hands at rest, weight slightly forward, neutral-attentive face. Voice low and unhurried.

**Cognitive load** (planning, analysis, reading Cosmic Awareness): hand-through-hair, middle-distance eye-rest, sometimes a slight tilt of the head 8–12° to the right. Speech, if any, slows to ~110 wpm. Body does not move otherwise.

**Stress, sub-threat** (Yon-Rogg in early issues, the Supreme Intelligence's manipulations): jaw masseter activates, blink rate drops, shoulders subtly square. Tongue-to-upper-teeth tell appears. He becomes *more polite*, not less — a Kree military convention that scales courtesy with hostility.

**Acute threat / combat**: the somatic profile inverts. He becomes faster, more decisive, more *kinetically present* than he is in any other state, but emotionally cooler. Voice rises in command register; breath deepens but does not quicken disproportionately. Eyes hard-track. No micro-gestures; the body is fully recruited.

**Grief** (Una; later, his own dying): right palm to sternum; long blinks; saccades shorten and dwell; voice drops in volume but not in pitch. He does not weep on-panel. Inferred: he weeps alone, briefly, with full somatic permission, and then stops — the same suppression-not-repression pattern §3 identified.

**Intimacy** (Una, Rick at his most vulnerable, Carol at the bedside, Wendy in the ward): shoulders drop, weight-bias releases to neutral, gaze rests rather than scans, voice softens, hand-initiated contact becomes possible. The body that does not fidget becomes the body that *holds*.

**Awe** (cosmic encounters, the Eon awakening, certain Thanos sequences): a rare full stillness in which even the breath suspends for two to three seconds; the inner-brow lifts; lips part very slightly. This is the only state in which his mouth opens without speech.

**Dying** (MGN #1): the baseline somatic discipline persists astonishingly far into the disease. He stands when standing is no longer reasonable. He keeps the forward weight-bias until the last days. The tremor in the hands rises; the saccades slow further; the long-closure blink generalizes. At the end, on the bed, what fails first is not the discipline but the substrate underneath it. The discipline is intact when the body stops.

---

## XI. SYNTHESIS

The somatic file describes a body that is a *trained instrument*, used economically, displayed minimally, and surrendered without protest. The catalog of presences (the hair-rake, the wrist-stroke, the palm-to-sternum, the long-closure blink) is small; the catalog of absences (no fidget, no vanity, no theatrics, no grooming-anxiety, no flinch) is large. This is the body of a man whose interior has organized itself sufficiently that the exterior does not need to leak. The few leaks that occur — and they are reliable, longitudinal, writer-independent — are the leaks of a man whose continence is chosen rather than constitutional, which is why they read as moving rather than as cold. A surveillance file built from this atlas would predict him with high accuracy and capture him with none.

*End somatic atlas. Continue to §4.3 — Routes, Rituals, Daily Architecture.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## I. Attachment Style — Classification and Origin

The subject's attachment configuration is best classified as **earned-secure with a persistent dismissing residue**, overlaid in the later years by what the trauma-attachment literature would call a *transcendent-protective* mode — bonds metabolized into stewardship rather than reciprocity. He is neither the avoidant who flees closeness nor the anxious who clutches at it; he is the kind of bonded adult who, having lost too much too early, learned to love by *carrying* rather than by *holding*.

The origin is overdetermined and traceable in three strata.

**Stratum one: Kree military socialization.** The Kree Imperial Militia is doctrinally a hierarchical culture that pathologizes affective display in male officers. Mar-Vell's earliest documented behaviors aboard the *Helion* — clipped address forms, rigid spatial discipline around superiors, suppression of facial affect in the presence of subordinates — show the standard-issue interior of a career officer in such a system. The dismissing residue almost certainly originates here: a default assumption that one's own emotional states are operationally irrelevant, that needs are managed privately, that intimacy is conducted in stolen interstitial moments (the early Una scenes consistently take place *between* duty intervals, never *instead of* them).

**Stratum two: the Yon-Rogg poisoning.** From the first mission, the subject's commanding officer is actively, covertly attempting to kill him over Una. This produces a very specific attachment lesion: it is not abandonment, not abuse, not neglect — it is the experience of *betrayal masked by legitimate authority*. The lesson encoded is structural: *institutions and their representatives may wear the face of trust while functioning as predator*. The behavioral consequence is durable and visible across the canon — he extends provisional trust to roles and ranks, but his real fidelity attaches only to individuals and principles he has tested.

**Stratum three: the Una loss and the Nega-Band fusion.** These compound. Una dies because of Yon-Rogg's engineered negligence; the Supreme Intelligence then binds him to Rick Jones via the Nega-Bands. The attachment system, still grieving, is forcibly conscripted into a new intimacy on terms he did not choose with a partner not of his species or generation. This is the formative event of his mature relational style: he learns, under duress, to *honor* a bond he did not elect, to *find* in it the textures of care, and to *not* permit the involuntariness to poison the warmth. This is the precise psychological skill that becomes his signature — the ability to take an obligation and inhabit it as love without ever lying to himself about its origin.

Earned-secure is the right label because the security was *constructed*, not inherited — visible through the Starlin arc as he integrates loss and obligation into a coherent caregiving identity. The dismissing residue persists in the form he never quite loses: a slight, automatic conversion of intimacy into responsibility, a preference for being the one who attends rather than the one attended to.

## II. The Bonding Cycle — How He Comes Close

The pattern, repeated with statistical reliability across the dossier, has five phases.

**Phase 1 — Operational adjacency.** Initial proximity is always *task-mediated*. He does not meet anyone socially; he meets them inside a mission, a crisis, a hospital corridor, a battlefield. Una was a unit medic. Rick Jones arrived as an emergency Nega-Band tether. Carol Danvers was a security officer at the Cape. Mentor and Eros were encountered in the Thanos campaign. Even the dying child Wendy in MGN #1 enters his life through the oncology ward, not through chosen sociality. The pattern is so consistent it functions as a screen: people he meets while *doing something* become candidates for bond; people he might meet at rest do not, because he is almost never at rest.

**Phase 2 — Calibrated observation.** He is a watcher before he is a participant. Early Una sequences show him noticing small things — her gait when off-duty, the way she holds a medical instrument, the micro-expressions she shows Yon-Rogg versus those she shows him. With Rick Jones the calibration is more pronounced and slightly anthropological: he is reading a human adolescent's emotional vocabulary in real time. With Carol Danvers there is an instructor's read — capability, attention, integrity. The calibration is never cold; he is looking for purchase points where he can offer something useful. The behavior maps onto what attachment researchers call *mentalizing* — extensive theory-of-mind work performed before commitment.

**Phase 3 — Offered utility as opening intimacy.** He does not say *I would like to know you better*. He provides. With Una, protective field-coverage during the *Helion* missions. With Rick, instruction in Nega-Band mechanics and an apologetic intimacy about the imposed sharing. With Carol, tactical mentorship and explanation of Kree biology. With Wendy, simply his time and presence — sitting on the edge of the bed, answering questions about cosmos and dying without condescension. Offered utility is his love language; the offer functions as the first declaration of care, and recipients who recognize it as such become candidates for deeper bond.

**Phase 4 — Disclosed weight.** Only after utility has been received does he disclose anything personal — and what he discloses is almost always *cosmological* rather than autobiographical. He will tell you what he believes about death before he tells you what he feels about his mother. With Una there is a documented sequence of him speaking about Hala's social fractures, the Pink/Blue caste resentment, the doctrinal ossification of the Supreme Intelligence — political-philosophical disclosure where another suitor would offer biographical confession. The recipient who absorbs this without flinching has now been admitted to the inner circle; the recipient who deflects it is quietly downgraded.

**Phase 5 — Conversion to stewardship.** The terminal phase of his bonding cycle is the moment the relationship is reclassified, in his interior accounting, from *companionship* to *charge*. This is the dismissing residue at work. Once he loves you, you become something he is responsible for. The reclassification is invisible to most partners but produces a characteristic shift: he begins making decisions on your behalf without consulting you, sometimes for your protection, sometimes for the protection of the bond itself. Una was protected from the full extent of his Yon-Rogg suspicions. Rick is repeatedly spared the full weight of what the Nega-Zone exile costs Mar-Vell. Carol is allowed to graduate from his tutelage before she might have asked to. Wendy is given a serenity about death he himself had to fight for.

The cycle is benign, even loving, and it is also a *closed system* — the loved one rarely gets to reciprocate the stewardship, because he does not present as needful.

## III. Distrust — How He Withholds and Why

Distrust in this subject is exceptionally well-managed and almost never theatrical. He does not perform suspicion; he documents it privately.

**Default posture toward authority:** provisional trust, withdrawn the moment evidence accumulates. With Yon-Rogg the early record shows him executing orders he already suspects are designed to kill him — he does not refuse, does not confront, but begins the silent accumulation of evidence. With the Supreme Intelligence the same: he serves until the directive to subjugate Earth crosses an ethical threshold, then refuses absolutely without escalation rhetoric. The pattern is *quiet non-compliance after long quiet evaluation*. He does not warn the institution he is about to leave it; he simply leaves, completely, when the evidence is sufficient.

**Default posture toward individuals:** generous baseline, narrow exclusion criteria. The exclusion criteria, derived from behavior across the canon, are roughly: cruelty to the defenseless, dishonesty about consequential matters, instrumentalization of intimacy. People who exhibit these are quietly downgraded to operational counterparts — he will still cooperate, still be civil, but the bond candidacy is closed. The downgrade is subtle and the person being downgraded almost never notices it has happened.

**Antithesis of paranoia.** What is striking is that the betrayals he has actually experienced — Yon-Rogg, the Kree state — did *not* produce generalized distrust. He distrusts the specific source and the specific class of behavior, not the world. He remains capable of meeting Skrulls without hostility (MGN #1's reconciliation), of negotiating with Thanos rather than reflexively striking, of accepting Eon's cosmic appointment without paranoid scrutiny of motive. This selectivity of distrust is itself a marker of integration; the unhealed traumatized person globalizes, while the healed one specifies.

## IV. Betrayal — Both Suffered and (Apparently) Committed

He is the betrayed, not the betrayer, but the file requires examination of both sides.

**As betrayed:** The Yon-Rogg sequence is the primary wound. The Supreme Intelligence's death sentence is the secondary. The Nega-Band fusion is structural betrayal by the Kree state masquerading as battlefield expedient. In each case the metabolization follows the same arc: brief, contained affective response (anger or grief, never both at full volume simultaneously); a period of operational adjustment; integration of the experience into a refined ethical position. He does not nurse betrayals. He extracts the lesson, restructures around it, and proceeds. Notably, he never seeks vengeance — the eventual confrontations with Yon-Rogg are dutiful rather than retributive, and the eventual rapprochement with the Kree state (their posthumous rehabilitation, which he learns of in the dying) is accepted without triumphalism.

**As betrayer (the inverse charge that adversaries levy):** The Kree formally categorize him as traitor. By the internal standards of the Imperial Militia, he is. The behavioral record shows he does not contest this designation morally — he accepts that within the Kree frame he is what they say he is — but he refuses the *valence* the Kree assign to it. He has, in his own ethical accounting, transferred fidelity from a corrupt sovereign to a worthier one (first Earth, then the cosmos, finally his own integrated conscience). The relational meaning: he is capable of leaving a relationship absolutely when it requires him to act against his principles, and the leaving will be quiet, complete, and unaccompanied by the destructive rhetoric most defectors generate. People who bond with him should understand this — *he will not betray them, but he will leave if they require betrayal of him*, and the leaving will be irrevocable.

## V. Repair — The Mechanics of Reconciliation

He is exceptionally good at repair, in a particular mode. The mode is *acknowledgment plus return to presence*, with no extended apology theater.

**With Rick Jones.** The Nega-Band binding produces recurring friction — Rick wants a life, Mar-Vell wants Rick to have a life, and the mechanics of the bond keep frustrating both. Repair episodes follow a consistent pattern: brief direct acknowledgment of the cost to Rick; concrete operational adjustment (training, exchange schedules, limits on combat exposure); resumption of the shared work with the affection slightly more visible than before. He does not over-apologize. He does not catastrophize the rupture. He treats the friction as a navigable feature of the bond rather than an indictment of it.

**With Carol Danvers.** When the mentor-student relationship begins to constrain her, his repair is essentially *release*. He stops mentoring before she stops needing it, slightly early rather than slightly late, and grants her the social space to become her own thing. There is some sublimation here — he likely would have preferred deeper continued contact — but the release is itself the repair.

**With the Kree.** The deathbed sequence in MGN #1 is the masterclass. When Kree representatives arrive to offer posthumous rehabilitation, he accepts it with grace, without exacting symbolic concession, without dwelling on the years of exile. He understands that institutions reconcile slowly and that demanding more than they can offer at any given moment will preclude the offering altogether. The repair is permitted to be incomplete because incompleteness is the realistic horizon.

**With the Skrulls.** The Skrull medal in MGN #1 is the most striking instance. After decades of war between his adopted Earth-allies and the Skrull Empire, he accepts an honor from his enemy on his deathbed, in a posture of pure peer respect. This is the repair faculty operating at maximum aperture: he is willing to recognize the dignity of an adversary even when that recognition costs him nothing because he is dying and everything when measured against the warrior identity he is being asked to set aside.

The signature of his repair behavior across all cases: *small ceremony, large substance*. He does not stage reconciliations; he enacts them.

## VI. Intimacy Patterns — Erotic, Familial, Brotherly

**Erotic intimacy** is documented essentially only through Una and, more abstractly, in the unconsummated longing-and-restraint registers around Carol Danvers. The Una relationship is the only fully realized romantic bond in the file, and it is characterized by an unusual register: *parallel companionship rather than fusion*. They do their jobs alongside each other; the love is communicated in small spatial gestures (positioning during briefings, the way they angle toward each other in the mess), in operational coverage (he runs cover for her on hazardous medical extractions), and in stolen brief dialogues that are remarkably *un-romantic* in vocabulary but emotionally complete. He loves her with the affect of a man who knows the universe is not safe and is determined to make a small region of safety around her. Her death does not extinguish this register; it transfers it. Subsequent romantic possibilities (the canon is sparse here, and what exists shows hesitation rather than pursuit) are met with a polite, unmistakable refusal. He has, in effect, decided that erotic intimacy is over for him, and he organizes life as a widower-monk thereafter.

**Familial intimacy** he generates rather than inherits. Hala-side family is functionally absent from the operational record. He constructs a chosen family — Rick as a kind of younger brother and forced twin, Carol as a younger sister and apprentice, Mentor and Eros as elder kin met cosmically, the dying child Wendy as the daughter he never had. The chosen family functions for him as a real one; he is loyal to it on the deepest registers. The fact that he had to *construct* it from professional contacts rather than receive it from origin is the dismissing-attachment residue's positive face: he has the relational skill to build kinship from the materials at hand.

**Brotherly intimacy** is his strongest register and where he is most fluent.
